2. Know the concept, not the name? → `sg_nls_search`


## Efficiency Rules

- Chain searches logically: search → read → references → definition
- Don't re-search for the same pattern; use results from prior calls
- Prefer `sg_keyword_search` over `sg_nls_search` when you have exact terms
- Read 2-3 related files before synthesising, rather than one at a time
- Don't read 20+ remote files without writing code — once you understand the pattern, start implementing

# Domain Lineage: Kafka Producer Config Propagation Path

## Your Task

Trace how the `acks` producer configuration value propagates through the Kafka codebase. Find all Java source files in `apache/kafka` that: 1. Define the `acks` configuration constant (in `ProducerConfig`). 2. Read and validate the `acks` value during producer initialization. 3. Encode the `acks` value into the produce request protocol (the `ProduceRequest` builder). 4. Apply the `acks` value in the broker-side partition leader to determine write acknowledgment behavior. Report the repo, file path, class name, and the role in the propagation chain for each file.

## Context

You are working on a codebase task involving repos from the domain domain.

## Available Resources

The local `/workspace/` directory contains: sg-evals/kafka--0753c489, sg-evals/flink--0cc95fcc, sg-evals/camel--1006f047.

**Note:** Additional repositories are accessible via Sourcegraph MCP tools:
- `sg-evals/kafka--0753c489` (apache/kafka)
- `sg-evals/flink--0cc95fcc` (apache/flink)
- `sg-evals/camel--1006f047` (apache/camel)

## Output Format

```json
{
```

56-assistanttext-
Perfect! I've successfully traced the `acks` producer configuration through the Kafka codebase and created a comprehensive answer file. Here's a summary of my findings:

## Summary of `acks` Configuration Propagation

**1. Configuration Definition** (ProducerConfig.java)
- Defines `ACKS_CONFIG = "acks"` constant
- Validates values with `parseAcks()` method (accepts 0, 1, "all"→-1)

**2. Producer Initialization** (KafkaProducer.java)
- Reads and parses the acks value from config
- Passes short value to Sender constructor

**3. Client-Side Transmission** (Sender.java)
- Stores acks as a field
- Encodes it into ProduceRequest via `setAcks(acks)` at line 899

**4. Protocol Definition** (ProduceRequest.json)
- Defines Acks as int16 field in the protocol specification

**5. Request Object** (ProduceRequest.java)
- Extracts acks from ProduceRequestData
- Provides acks() getter method

**6. Broker Reception** (KafkaApis.scala)
- Receives produce request and passes acks as `requiredAcks` parameter to ReplicaManager

**7. Broker Validation** (ReplicaManager.scala)
- Validates requiredAcks (-1, 1, or 0 only)
- Uses it to determine if delayed produce is needed when requiredAcks == -1

**8. Write Acknowledgment Enforcement** (Partition.scala)
- Partition leader checks if requiredAcks == -1 and enforces min.isr requirement
- Rejects writes if ISR is too small for "all" acks durability guarantee

The complete lineage has been saved to `/workspace/answer.json` with all files, symbols, and detailed narrative explanation.

Available options are:\\\" +\\n312:             \\\"<ul>\\\" +\\n313:             \\\"<li>If not set, the default partitioning logic is used. \\\" +\\n314:             \\\"This strategy send records to a partition until at least \\\" + BATCH_SIZE_CONFIG + \\\" bytes is produced to the partition. Note: There's a known issue that will cause uneven distribution when a new batch is created. \\\" +\\n323:             \\\"See KAFKA-9965 for more detail.\\\" +\\n324:             \\\"</li>\\\" +\\n325:             \\\"</ul>\\\" +\\n326:             \\\"<p>Implementing the <code>org.apache.kafka.clients.producer.Partitioner</code> interface allows you to plug in a custom partitioner.\\\";\\n327: \\n328:     /** <code>interceptor.classes</code> */\\n329:     public static final String INTERCEPTOR_CLASSES_CONFIG = \\\"interceptor.classes\\\";\\n330:     public static final String INTERCEPTOR_CLASSES_DOC = \\\"A list of classes to use as interceptors. \\\"\\n331:                                                         + \\\"Implementing the <code>org.apache.kafka.clients.producer.ProducerInterceptor</code> interface allows you to intercept (and possibly mutate) the records \\\"\\n332:                                                         + \\\"received by the producer before they are published to the Kafka cluster. This helps performance on both the client and the server. This configuration controls the \"\n84:                                                  + \"default batch size in bytes. \"\n85:                                                  + \"<p>\"\n86:                                                  + \"No attempt will be made to batch records larger than this size. \"\n87:                                                  + \"<p>\"\n88:                                                  + \"Requests sent to brokers will contain multiple batches, one for each partition with data available to be sent. \"\n89:                                                  + \"<p>\"\n90:                                                  + \"A small batch size will make batching less common and may reduce throughput (a batch size of zero will disable \"\n91:                                                  + \"batching entirely). A very large batch size may use memory a bit more wastefully as we will always allocate a \"\n92:                                                  + \"buffer of the specified batch size in anticipation of additional records.\"\n93:                                                  + \"<p>\"\n94:                                                  + \"Note: This setting gives the upper bound of the batch size to be sent. If we have fewer than this many bytes accumulated \"\n95:                                                  + \"for this partition, we will 'linger' for the <code>linger.ms</code> time waiting for more records to show up. \"\n96:                                                  + \"This <code>linger.ms</code> setting defaults to 5, which means the producer will wait for 5ms or until the record batch is \"\n97:                                                  + \"of <code>batch.size</code> (whichever happens first) before sending the record batch. Note that broker backpressure can \"\n98:                                                  + \" result in a higher effective linger time than this setting. \"\n99:                                                  + \"The default changed from 0 to 5 in Apache Kafka 4.0 as the efficiency gains from larger batches typically result in \"\n100:                                                  + \"similar or lower producer latency despite the increased linger.\";\n101: \n102:     /** <code>partitioner.adaptive.partitioning.enable</code> */\n103:     public static final String PARTITIONER_ADPATIVE_PARTITIONING_ENABLE_CONFIG = \"partitioner.adaptive.partitioning.enable\";\n104:     private static final String PARTITIONER_ADPATIVE_PARTITIONING_ENABLE_DOC =\n105:             \"When set to 'true', the producer will try to adapt to broker performance and produce more messages to partitions hosted on faster brokers. \"\n106:             + \"If 'false', the producer will try to distribute messages uniformly. This controls the \"\n125:                                            + \" durability of records that are sent. The following settings are allowed: \"\n126:                                            + \" <ul>\"\n127:                                            + \" <li><code>acks=0</code> If set to zero then the producer will not wait for any acknowledgment from the\"\n128:                                            + \" server at all. The record will be immediately added to the socket buffer and considered sent. No guarantee can be\"\n129:                                            + \" made that the server has received the record in this case, and the <code>retries</code> configuration will not\"\n130:                                            + \" take effect (as the client won't generally know of any failures). The offset given back for each record will\"\n131:                                            + \" always be set to <code>-1</code>.\"\n132:                                            + \" <li><code>acks=1</code> This will mean the leader will write the record to its local log but will respond\"\n133:                                            + \" without awaiting full acknowledgement from all followers. In this case should the leader fail immediately after\"\n134:                                            + \" acknowledging the record but before the followers have replicated it then the record will be lost.\"\n135:                                            + \" <li><code>acks=all</code> This means the leader will wait for the full set of in-sync replicas to\"\n136:                                            + \" acknowledge the record. This guarantees that the record will not be lost as long as at least one in-sync replica\"\n137:                                            + \" remains alive. This is the strongest available guarantee. This is equivalent to the acks=-1 setting.\"\n138:                                            + \"</ul>\"\n139:                                            + \"<p>\"\n140:                                            + \"Note that enabling idempotence requires this config value to be 'all'.\"\n141:                                            + \" If conflicting configurations are set and idempotence is not explicitly enabled, idempotence is disabled.\";\n142: \n143:     /** <code>linger.ms</code> */\n144:     public static final String LINGER_MS_CONFIG = \"linger.ms\";\n145:     private static final String LINGER_MS_DOC = \"The producer groups together any records that arrive in between request transmissions into a single batched request. \"\n146:                                                 + \"Normally this occurs only under load when records arrive faster than they can be sent out. However in some circumstances the client may want to \"\n147:                                                 + \"reduce the number of requests even under moderate load. This setting accomplishes this by adding a small amount \"\n148:                                                 + \"of artificial delay&mdash;that is, rather than immediately sending out a record, the producer will wait for up to \"\n149:                                                 + \"the given delay to allow other records to be sent so that the sends can be batched together. This can be thought \"\n150:                                                 + \"of as analogous to Nagle's algorithm in TCP. This setting gives the upper bound on the delay for batching: once \"\n151:                                                 + \"we get <code>\" + BATCH_SIZE_CONFIG + \"</code> worth of records for a partition it will be sent immediately regardless of this \"\n152:                                                 + \"setting, however if we have fewer than this many bytes accumulated for this partition we will 'linger' for the \"\n153:                                                 + \"specified time waiting for more records to show up. This setting defaults to 5 (i.e. 5ms delay). Increasing <code>\" + LINGER_MS_CONFIG + \"=50</code>, \"\n154:                                                 + \"for example, would have the effect of reducing the number of requests sent but would add up to 50ms of latency to records sent in the absence of load.\"\n155:                                                 + \"The default changed from 0 to 5 in Apache Kafka 4.0 as the efficiency gains from larger batches typically result in \"\n156:                                                 + \"similar or lower producer latency despite the increased linger.\";\n157: \n158:     /** <code>request.timeout.ms</code> */\n159:     public static final String REQUEST_TIMEOUT_MS_CONFIG = CommonClientConfigs.REQUEST_TIMEOUT_MS_CONFIG;\n160:     private static final String REQUEST_TIMEOUT_MS_DOC = CommonClientConfigs.REQUEST_TIMEOUT_MS_DOC\n161:         + \" This should be larger than <code>replica.lag.time.max.ms</code> (a broker configuration)\"\n162:         + \" to reduce the possibility of message duplication due to unnecessary producer retries.\";\n163: \n164:     /** <code>delivery.timeout.ms</code> */\n165:     public static final String DELIVERY_TIMEOUT_MS_CONFIG = \"delivery.timeout.ms\";\n166:     private static final String DELIVERY_TIMEOUT_MS_DOC = \"An upper bound on the time to report success or failure \"\n167:             + \"after a call to <code>send()</code> returns.
